100 1 $aBode, Irwin Theodore,$d1891-
245 14$aThe shelterbelt as an asset on the Iowa farm /$cby I.T. Bode.
260 0 $a[Ames, Iowa :$bIowa State College of Agriculture and Mechanic Arts, Extension Service, Agriculture and Home Economics,$c1922]
300   $a16 p. :$bill. ;$c22 cm.
490 0 $aExtension Service bulletin ;$vno.108
520 8 $a"No farmstead is complete without a shelterbelt protection for its buildings and farm lots. Wherever native timber of existing plantings do not furnish this protection, permanent plantings of some sort should be established. Experience shows that, even before such plantings reach a height sufficient to afford much protection, they add enough to the sale value of the farm more than to pay for the trouble it took to put them in. The value of the shelterbelt cannot be measured by the value of the land it occupies. It must be put into the dollars and cents value of increased gains in livestock, better health and living conditions for both man and animals, decreased fuel bills, additional sale value for the farm, and other items like these."--Page [1].
